Amino acid sequences from each OG were first aligned with MAFFT [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 95" title="Katoh K, Misawa K, Kuma KI, Miyata T. MAFFT: a novel method for rapid multiple sequence alignment based on fast fourier transform. Nucleic Acids Res. 2002;30:305966." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR95" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4118">95</a>]; the alignments were then adjusted manually and ambiguous positions were deleted with TrimAI [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 96" title="Capella-Gutierrez S, Silla-Martinez JM, Gabaldon T. trimAl: A tool for automated alignment trimming in large-scale phylogenetic analyses. Bioinformatics. 2009;25:19723." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR96" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4121">96</a>]. Then, the sequence alignments were concatenated. Finally, the concatenated alignment was used to construct a maximum likelihood (ML) phylogenetic tree using IQ-TREE software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 97" title="Nguyen LT, Schmidt HA, von Haeseler A, Minh BQ. IQ-TREE: a fast and effective stochastic algorithm for estimating maximum-likelihood phylogenies. Mol Biol Evol. 2015;32:26874." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR97" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4124">97</a>].</p><p>We estimated the divergence time of species using MCMCTree [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Yang ZH, Rannala B. Bayesian estimation of species divergence times under a molecular clock using multiple fossil calibrations with soft bounds. Mol Biol Evol. 2006;23:21226." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4130">37</a>] and BEAST2 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Bouckaert R, Heled J, Khnert D, Vaughan T, Wu CH, et al. BEAST 2: a software platform for bayesian evolutionary analysis. PLoS Comput Biol. 2014;10:e1003537." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4133">38</a>]. For the age estimation using MCMCTree, the tree was calibrated with angiosperm crown age (209 million years ago, MYA) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Li HT, Yi TS, Gao ML, Ma PF, Zhang T, Yang JB, et al. Origin of angiosperms and the puzzle of the jurassic gap. Nat Plants. 2019;5:46170." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4136">36</a>], eudicot crown age range (127.9139.4 MYA), and <i>Theobroma cacaoArabidopsis thaliana</i> divergence range (8795 MYA). The latter two calibrated times were obtained from TreeTime [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 98" title="Kumar S, Stecher G, Suleski M, Hedges SB. Timetree: a resource for timelines, timetrees, and divergence times. Mol Biol Evol. 2017;34:18129." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR98" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4142">98</a>]. For the age estimation using BEAST [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Bouckaert R, Heled J, Khnert D, Vaughan T, Wu CH, et al. BEAST 2: a software platform for bayesian evolutionary analysis. PLoS Comput Biol. 2014;10:e1003537." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4146">38</a>], the earliest tricolpate pollen (~125 MYA) fossil associated with eudicots and the fossil (100.5 MYA) assigned to the Pentapetalae were used as calibration points. The angiosperm crown age of 209 MYA [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Li HT, Yi TS, Gao ML, Ma PF, Zhang T, Yang JB, et al. Origin of angiosperms and the puzzle of the jurassic gap. Nat Plants. 2019;5:46170." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4149">36</a>] was also used as a calibration point.</p><p>Expansion and contractions of gene families were determined using CAFE 2.2 (Computational Analysis of Gene Family Evolution) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="De Bie T, Cristianini N, Demuth JP, Hahn MW. CAFE: a computational tool for the study of gene family evolution. Bioinformatics. 2006;22:126971." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4155">39</a>]. The program uses a birth and death process to model gene gain and loss over a phylogeny. Enrichment of KEGG and Gene Ontology terms for <i>T. sinense</i> or <i>T. aralioides</i> gene families that rapidly evolved (expanded or contracted rapidly) were performed using goseq [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 99" title="Young MD, Wakefield MJ, Smyth GK, Oshlack A. Gene ontology analysis for RNA-seq: accounting for selection bias. Genome Biol. 2010;11:R14." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR99" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4164">99</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec26">Whole-genome duplication analysis</h3><p>We performed intragenomic comparisons for the two species of Trochodendraceae, <i>Aquilegia coerulea</i>, <i>Nelumbo nucifera</i>, and <i>Vitis vinifera</i>. We also performed intergenomic comparisons between <i>T. sinense</i> or <i>T. aralioides</i> and several species including two basal angiosperms (<i>Amborella trichopoda</i> and <i>Nymphaea colorata</i>), one magnoliid (<i>Cinnamomum kanehirae</i>), two early diverging eudicots (<i>A. coerulea</i>, <i>N. nucifera</i>), and one core eudicot (<i>Vitis vinifera</i>)<i>.</i> OrthoFinder v2.3.1 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Emms DM, Kelly S. OrthoFinder: solving fundamental biases in whole genome comparisons dramatically improves orthogroup inference accuracy. Genome Biol. 2015;16:157. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1186/s13059-015-0721-2&#xA;                  &#xA;                ." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4213">35</a>] was used to identify paralogous gene pairs within species and orthologs between species. Based on these paralogous and orthologous gene pairs, collinear blocks were identified using MCsanX [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 100" title="Wang Y, Tang H, Debarry JD, Tan X, Li J, Wang X, et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 2012;40:e49." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR100" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4216">100</a>]. Protein sequences of paralogous and orthologous gene pairs in collinear blocks were first aligned by MUSCLE [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 101" title="Edgar RC. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 2004;32:17927." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR101" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4219">101</a>]. The protein alignments were then converted to codon alignments by PAL2NAL [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 102" title="Suyama M, Torrents D, Bork P. PAL2NAL: robust conversion of protein sequence alignments into the corresponding codon alignments. Nucleic Acids Res. 2006;34:W60912." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR102" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4222">102</a>]. Finally, <i>Ks</i> values were calculated using the Nei-Gojobori algorithm implemented in the PAML package [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 103" title="Yang Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol Biol Evol. 2007;24:158691." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR103" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4229">103</a>].</p><p>To confirm the timing of these WGDs in early diverging eudicots, we further performed integrated syntenic and phylogenomic analyses. We obtained anchor genes from the inter-genomic synteny blocks present in ratios of 1:2:4 in <i>A. trichopoda</i>, <i>N. nucifera</i>, and <i>T. sinense</i>. All genes in the same sets of syntenic blocks were concatenated. These concatenated datasets were used to perform phylogenetic analysis. We then calculated the percentage of trees that supported the idea that the WGDs in <i>N. nucifera</i> and <i>T. sinense</i> are lineage-specific.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec27">Timing of WGD events</h3><p>We first calculated the <i>Ks</i> value of the orthologs in syntenic regions between <i>T. sinense</i> and <i>T. aralioides</i> using KaKs_Caculator [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 104" title="Wang D, Zhang Y, Zhang Z, Zhu J, Yu J. KaKs_Calculator 2.0: a toolkit incorporating gamma-series methods and sliding window strategies. Genom Proteom Bioinf. 2010;8:7780." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR104" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4268">104</a>] based on the YN model. Given the median <i>Ks</i> value (0.2) of <i>T. sinense</i> and <i>T. aralioides</i> and their divergence date T (30.7 MYA), we calculated the synonymous substitutions per site per year (<i>r</i>) for Trochodendraceae as equaling 3.25e9 (<i>r</i>=<i>Ks</i>/2T).</p><p>We then applied the <i>r</i> value (3.25e9) to estimate the time of the Trochodendraceae WGD events (<i>T</i>=<i>Ks</i>/2r). Since the median <i>Ks</i> values of paralogous pairs of <i>T. sinense</i> corresponding to the two WGDs were 0.532 and 0.382, we estimated that the two WGDs occurred around 82 and 59 MYA. Based on the median <i>Ks</i> of paralogous pairs of <i>T. aralioides</i> corresponding the two WGDs (0.507 and 0.348), we dated the two WGDs to around 78 and 54 MYA. The small difference in time of the two WGDs in the Trochodendraceae inferred from these two species may be due to a difference in their evolution rates.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec28">Light microscopy</h3><p>Sectioning blocks of <i>T. sinense</i> [1cm (<i>L</i>)1cm (<i>R</i>)1cm (<i>T</i>)] were cut with razor blades and then softened in 2% ethylenediamine at 60C for 2days. Fifteen-micrometer-thick transverse, radial, and tangential sections were cut with a sliding microtome. Thereafter, sections were stained sequentially with 1% aqueous safranin solution, rinsed, and finally mounted beneath cover slides. Images were captured by a light microscope (Olympus BX50, Japan).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec29">Examination of secondary xylem with SEM</h3><p>For scanning electron microscope (SEM) analysis, the stem materials from <i>T. sinense</i> were collected from the upper slope of Fenshuiling, Yunnan province, China. Stem samples were boiled in water and sectioned on a sliding microtome, then cut into pieces about 1cm in length and fixed overnight in 2.5% glutaraldehyde, followed by washing with 0.1M PBS (pH7.2) three times. After sequential dehydration in 30%, 60%, 80%, 90%, 95%, and 100% ethyl alcohol (15min each), the samples were incubated in liquid carbon dioxide at 0C and 20C sequentially (20min each), then subjected to critical point drying at 35C for 15min using a Tousimis autosamdri-825 critical point dryer. Vacuum coating was performed using a HITACHI MC 10003 Sputter Coater under 10Pa and 1000V for 2min. The images were taken with an accelerating voltage of 510kV using a Hitachi SU80202 SEM.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec30">MicroCT imaging</h3><p>Wood blocks of <i>T. sinense</i> were imaged by X-ray microtomography using a Bruker Skyscan microCT system 1172 (Skyscan, Belgium) with a 20100kV, 10W X-ray source. The microCT device was set to operate at a voltage of 33kV and power of 7W. The sample was scanned at a voxel size resolution of 1.792m. The software Skyscans NRecon program (Skyscan, Belgium) was used to perform the reconstruction of the projection images, resulting in a volume of 330433041806m from 1032 slice images with a resolution of 188818881086 pixels each. Imaris volume rendering and analysis software (Imaris 64 9.0.1, BITPLANE, Oxford Instruments company) was used to render images from the three-dimensional data set.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec31">Gene family analysis</h3><p><i>AtVND7</i>, <i>AtLBD18/AtLBD30</i>, <i>AtMYB46</i>/<i>AtMYB83</i>, <i>AtCESA4</i>, <i>AtCESA8</i>, and <i>AtXCP1</i>/<i>AtXCP2</i> are key genes involved in the development of vessel elements in <i>A. thaliana</i> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Yamaguchi M, Mitsuda N, Ohtani M, Ohme-Takagi M, Kato K, Demura T. VASCULAR-RELATED NAC-DOMAIN 7 directly regulates the expression of a broad range of genes for xylem vessel formation. Plant J. 2011;66:57990." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4392">21</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Zhong R, Ye Z-H. Complexity of the transcriptional network controlling secondary wall biosynthesis. Plant Sci. 2014;229:193207." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4395">49</a>]<i>.</i> These genes belong to the <i>VNS</i>, <i>LBD</i>, <i>R2R3-MYB</i>, <i>CesA</i>, and <i>PLCP</i> gene families [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ohtani M, Nishikubo N, Xu B, Yamaguchi M, Mitsuda N, Goue N, et al. A NAC domain protein family contributing to the regulation of wood formation in poplar. Plant J. 2011;67:499512." href="#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4417">45</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Matsumura Y, Iwakawa H, Machida Y, Machida C. Characterization of genes in the ASYMMETRIC LEAVES2/LATERAL ORGAN BOUNDARIES (AS2/LOB) family in Arabidopsis thaliana, and functional and molecular comparisons between AS2 and other family members. Plant J. 2009;58:52537." href="#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4417_1">46</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Dubos C, Stracke R, Grotewold E, Weisshaar B, Martin C, Lepiniec L. MYB transcription factors in Arabidopsis. Trends Plant Sci. 2010;15:57381." href="#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4417_2">47</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Richau KH, Kaschani F, Verdoes M, Pansuriya TC, Niessen S, Stueber K, et al. Subclassification and biochemical analysis of plant papain-like cysteine proteases displays subfamily-specific characteristics. Plant Physiol. 2012;158:158399." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4421">48</a>], respectively. To investigate the evolutionary history of these gene families and identify the <i>T. sinense</i> genes orthologs, genes of <i>VNS</i>, <i>LBD</i>, <i>CesA</i>, and <i>PLCP</i> gene families from 22 representatives of major plant lineages, including 19 species of angiosperms used in the phylogenetic analysis of species, 3 gymnosperms (<i>Ginkgo biloba</i>, <i>Gnetum montanum</i>, and <i>Picea abies</i>), 1 lycophyte (<i>Selaginella moellendorffii</i>), and 1 moss (<i>Physcomitrella patens/ Physcomitrium patens</i>), were obtained using the hmmsearch command in the HMMER package [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 105" title="Finn RD, Clements J, Eddy SR. HMMER web server: interactive sequence similarity searching. Nucleic Acids Res. 2011;39:W2937." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR105" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4455">105</a>] with their specific Pfam models (Extended Data Information). <i>R2R3-MYB</i> transcription factor homologs were obtained by a BLASTp search with e-value 1e5 (Extended Data Information). Then, identical and defective sequences were identified and manually eliminated in BioEdit. Protein sequences or nucleotide sequences were aligned using MAFFT [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 95" title="Katoh K, Misawa K, Kuma KI, Miyata T. MAFFT: a novel method for rapid multiple sequence alignment based on fast fourier transform. Nucleic Acids Res. 2002;30:305966." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR95" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4462">95</a>] and the alignment was manually adjusted in BioEdit. Maximum likelihood trees were constructed using IQ-TREE software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 97" title="Nguyen LT, Schmidt HA, von Haeseler A, Minh BQ. IQ-TREE: a fast and effective stochastic algorithm for estimating maximum-likelihood phylogenies. Mol Biol Evol. 2015;32:26874." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR97" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4465">97</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec32">Plasmid construction and transient infiltration</h3><p>To investigate the subcellular localization of the VNDs, we created transgenic plants expressing <i>At</i>VND6, <i>At</i>VND7, <i>Ts</i>VND6.1, <i>Ts</i>VND6.2, and <i>Ts</i>VND7.2 fusions with GFP. To this end, the <i>AtVND6</i>, <i>AtVND7</i>, <i>TsVND6.1</i>, <i>TsVND6.2</i>, and <i>TsVND7.2</i> coding region fragments were amplified from wild-type (WT) complementary DNA (cDNA) of <i>A. thaliana</i> and <i>T. sinense</i> by using PCR with gene-specific primer sets (Supplementary Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#MOESM1">4</a>). After that, the cDNAs were each subcloned into a modified pCAMBIA 2300-GFP vector under the control of the 35S promoter to generate the <i>35S::AtVND6-GFP</i>, <i>35S::AtVND7-GFP</i>, <i>35S::TsVND6.1-GFP</i>, <i>35S::TsVND6.2-GFP</i>, and <i>35S::TsVND7.2-GFP</i> constructs. Transient infiltration of <i>Nicotiana benthamiana</i> was carried out using an <i>Agrobacterium tumefaciens</i> (GV3101). Images were captured using a Zeiss LSM 880 Airyscan (Carl Zeiss, Germany) for confocal microscopy. An argon laser (488-nm line) was used for GFP excitation and the emission was captured at 510550nm (green).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec33">Yeast one-hybrid analysis</h3><p>Yeast one-hybrid analysis was performed to investigate the interactions between <i>Ts</i>VND6.1, <i>Ts</i>VND7.1, <i>Ts</i>VND7.2 or <i>Ts</i>LBD30a transcription factors and the promoters of <i>TsVND7.2</i>, <i>TsMYB</i>, <i>TsCesA4</i>, <i>TsCesA8</i>, <i>TsXCPa</i>, <i>TsXCPb</i>, and <i>TsXCPc</i> (about 500bp in length from the translation start site). All the promoters and transcription factor genes were amplified by PCR using TransStart FastPfu DNA polymerase (TransGenBiotech, Beijing, China). Using BamHI/EcoRI or EcoRI/SacI digestion and T4 ligation reactions, the transcription factor genes were inserted into the AD vector (pGADT7, Takara Clontech Co., Ltd.) and the promoters were inserted into the BD vector (pHIS2, Takara Clontech Co., Ltd.). Then, the vectors were transformed into yeast strain Y187 and the transformed yeast was cultured for 23days on SD/-Trp/-His double deficiency medium. Single clones harboring different vector combinations were transferred to SD/-THL medium containing 10, 20, 30, 40, 50, and 60mM 3-AT and incubated at 30C for 0.58h, and the color changes in the yeast cells were observed. All primers are shown in Table S5 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#MOESM1">1</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec34">Luciferase activity assay</h3><p>To assay the activating activity of <i>Ts</i>VND6.1, <i>Ts</i>VND7.1, <i>Ts</i>VND7.2, <i>Ts</i>LBD30a, and <i>Ts</i>LBD30b to the <i>TsVND7.1, TsVND7.2</i>, <i>TsMYB</i>, <i>TsCesA4</i>, <i>TsCesA8</i>, <i>TsXCPa</i>, <i>TsXCPb</i>, and <i>TsXCPc</i> promoters, the pGreenII 0800-LUC reporter vector and pGreenII 62-SK effector vector (Biovector Science Lab) were used. The <i>TsVND7.1</i>, <i>TsVND7.2</i>, <i>TsMYB</i>, <i>TsCesA4</i>, <i>TsCesA8</i>, <i>TsXCPa</i>, <i>TsXCPb</i>, and <i>TsXCPc</i> promoters were cloned into pGreenII 0800 at the HindIII and BamHI sites to fuse them with the <i>LUC</i> reporter gene (<i>TsVND7.1</i>, <i>TsVND7.2</i>, <i>TsMYB</i>, <i>TsCesA4</i>, <i>TsCesA8</i>, <i>TsXCPa</i>, <i>TsXCPb</i>, or <i>TsXCPc</i> pro-LUC). The coding sequences for <i>Ts</i>VND6.1, <i>Ts</i>VND7.1, <i>Ts</i>VND7.2, <i>Ts</i>LBD30a, and <i>Ts</i>LBD30b were cloned into the pGreenII 62-SK vector at the EcoRI and HindIII sites. The recombinant vectors were co-transformed into <i>A. tumefaciens</i> GV3101. After centrifugation, the bacteria were collected and resuspended at A<sub>600</sub>=0.6 in infection solution (10mM MES, 10mM MgCl<sub>2</sub>, and 200M acetosyringone) for infiltration. The prepared suspensions were infiltrated into <i>N. benthamiana</i> leaves and grown in the dark for 48h. The leaves were then sprayed with luciferin and kept in the dark for 10min to quench the fluorescence. A CCD imaging apparatus (NightOWL LB 983 NC100, Berthold Technologies GmbH &amp; Co. KG, Bad Wildbad) was used for image capture.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec35">Resequencing</h3><p>DNA of 55 individuals from 6 populations, which represent most of the known distribution of <i>T. sinense</i> trees, was extracted and sequenced using Illumina technology. Raw data were filtered using Fastq [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 106" title="Chen S, Zhou Y, Chen Y, Gu J. Fastp: An ultra-fast all-in-one FASTQ preprocessor. Bioinformatics. 2018;34:88490." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR106" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4723">106</a>]. Clean reads were aligned to the <i>T. sinense</i> genome using BWA-MEM [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Li H. Aligning sequence reads, clone sequences and assembly contigs with BWA-MEM. arXiv. 2013:arXiv:1303.3997v2." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4729">81</a>]. Duplicate reads were marked with sambamba-markdup [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 107" title="Tarasov A, Vilella AJ, Cuppen E, Nijman IJ, Prins P, et al. Sambamba: fast processing of NGS alignment formats. Bioinformatics. 2015;31:20324." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR107" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4732">107</a>]. FreeBayes [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 108" title="Garrison E, Marth G. Haplotype-based variant detection from short-read sequencing. arXiv. 2012:arXiv:1207.3907v2." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR108" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4736">108</a>] was used to conduct SNP calling.</p><p>Ancestry estimation of individuals was inferred using ADMIXTURE [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Alexander DH, Novembre J, Lange K. Fast model-based estimation of ancestry in unrelated individuals. Genome Res. 2009;19:165564." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4742">50</a>] with different values of <i>K</i> (<i>K</i>=1 to 10). We performed 5-fold cross-validation to determine the most likely number of clusters. The GCTA tool [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 109" title="Yang J, Lee SH, Goddard ME, Visscher PM. GCTA: a tool for genome-wide complex trait analysis. Am J Hum Genet. 2011;88:7682." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR109" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4751">109</a>] was used to generate genetic relationship matrix (GRM) files and the GRM file was used to compute principal components (PCs). We constructed a neighbor-joining (NJ) phylogenetic tree using MEGA7 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 110" title="Kumar S, Stecher G, Tamura K. Mega7: molecular evolutionary genetics analysis version 7.0 for bigger datasets. Mol Biol Evol. 2016;33:18704." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR110" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4754">110</a>] based on the whole-genome SNPs of the 55 individuals. Branch support was estimated from 1000 bootstrap replicates. <i>T. aralioides</i> was used as an outgroup.</p><p>Population genetic parameters, including nucleotide diversity () [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 111" title="Nei M, Li WH. Mathematical model for studying genetic variation in terms of restriction endonucleases. Proc Natl Acad Sci. 1979;76:526973." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR111" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4764">111</a>] and the Watterson estimator (w) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 112" title="Watterson GA. On the number of segregating sites in genetical models without recombination. Theor Popul Biol. 1975;7:25676." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR112" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4767">112</a>], were used to measure the degree of variability within a population or species and Fst (fixation index) was used to measure the degree of genetic differentiation, which was calculated using the thetaStat command of ANGSD softpackage [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 113" title="Korneliussen TS, Albrechtsen A, Nielsen R. ANGSD: analysis of next generation sequencing data. BMC Bioinformatics. 2014;15:336." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR113" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4770">113</a>] over non-overlapping 20-kb windows. To estimate gene flow between populations, we performed Treemix v1.13 on the SNPs with the settings -se -bootstrap -k 500 -m, and values for (-m) ranging from 1 to 10. We applied the stairway plot [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 114" title="Liu X, Fu YX. Exploring population size changes using SNP frequency spectra. Nat Genet. 2015;47:5559." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR114" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4773">114</a>] to the whole-genome sequences of nine populations to infer the historical effective population size. The estimated generation time and mutation rate were set to 15 and 2.745e9, respectively.</p></div></div></section>
                    <section aria-labelledby="availability-of-data-and-materials" data-title="Availability of data and materials"><div class="c-article-section" id="availability-of-data-and-materials-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="availability-of-data-and-materials">Availability of data and materials</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="availability-of-data-and-materials-content">
              
              <p>All raw sequencing reads generated in this study have been deposited to the NCBI Sequence Read Archive (<a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra">https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra</a>) with Bioproject accession number PRJNA625382 (<a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/PRJNA625382">https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/PRJNA625382</a>) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 115" title="Liu P-L, Zhang X, Mao J-F, Hong Y-M, Zhang R-G, E YL, et al. NCBI Sequence Read Archive, &#xA;                  https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/PRJNA625382&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2020)." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7#ref-CR115" id="ref-link-section-d33374e4855">115</a>]. The genome assembly sequences and gene annotations have been deposited at DDBJ/ENA/GenBank under the accession JABCRI010000000. Original images of <i>T. sinense</i> captured from field and original figures captured from microCT used for cell parameters analysis have been deposited to the figshare online database (<a href="https://doi.org/10.6084/m9.figshare.13159991.v2">https://doi.org/10.6084/m9.figshare.13159991.v2</a>) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 116" title="Lin JX; Zhang X; Liu P-L: Original images of Tetracentron sinense. Figshare.                         <span class="c-article-identifiers"><a class="c-article-identifiers__item" href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=search&amp;term=Jinxing+Lin" data-track="click" data-track-action="author link - pubmed" data-track-label="link">PubMed</a><span class="u-hide"></span><a class="c-article-identifiers__item" href="http://scholar.google.co.uk/scholar?as_q=&amp;num=10&amp;btnG=Search+Scholar&amp;as_epq=&amp;as_oq=&amp;as_eq=&amp;as_occt=any&amp;as_sauthors=%22Jinxing+Lin%22&amp;as_publication=&amp;as_ylo=&amp;as_yhi=&amp;as_allsubj=all&amp;hl=en" data-track="click" data-track-action="author link - scholar" data-track-label="link">Google Scholar</a></span></p></div></div></li></ol></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="contributions">Contributions</h3><p>JXL and YNJ conceived and planned the project. P-LL, XZ, J-FM, and Y-MH are the lead investigators and contributed equally to the work. P-LL, R-G Z, J-FM, CKJ, SHN, JBX, and LX managed and coordinated all the bioinformatics activities surrounding assembly, quality control, set-up, and maintenance of <i>Tetracentron sinense</i>. YLE, QZHH, and WQZ constructed the vector for overexpression and GFP fusion protein transgenic plants. XZ carried out the yeast one-hybrid assay. XZ and Y-MH performed the microCT experiment. WWS, Y-MH, and HMX performed the wood maceration and contributed to the scanning electron microscope imaging. SN, KHJ, JH, and XCT participated in bioinformatics data analysis. XMJ, YFY, and BL prepared and produced most of the wood sections. YPM contributed to material preparation and collection. SA, PKJ, LW, BJ, ZBQ, FB, J, and XQH helped in correcting the manuscript. C-JL, HZK, SG, and RAD revised the manuscript and provided suggestions for experimental design and project direction. All authors contributed to the writing of the paper and commented on the manuscript. P-LL, XZ, J-FM, and Y-MH contributed equally. Correspondence and requests for materials should be addressed to JXL. The authors read and approved the final manuscript.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
                <a id="corresp-c1" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7/email/correspondent/c1/new">Yuannian Jiao</a> or <a id="corresp-c2" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-02198-7/email/correspondent/c2/new">Jinxing Lin</a>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="ethics" data-title="Ethics declarations"><div class="c-article-section" id="ethics-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="ethics">Ethics declarations</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="ethics-content">
